â”‚  WHY LAYERING MATTERS:                                                      â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Separation of concerns - each layer has one job                          â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Maintainability - changes isolated to specific layers                    â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Testability - layers can be tested independently                         â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Team organization - teams can own specific layers                        â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Replaceability - swap implementations without affecting others           â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  KEY OPTIMIZATION TIPS:                                                     â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Enforce strict dependency direction (top to bottom only)                 â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Use interfaces at layer boundaries                                       â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Keep layers focused on their specific responsibility                     â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Don't skip layers (avoid presentation calling data directly)             â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Use DTOs to decouple layer data representations                          â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Apply dependency inversion for infrastructure dependencies               â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Consider vertical slices for feature organization                        â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  COMMON PITFALLS TO AVOID:                                                  â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Anemic domain model (all logic in services)                              â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Leaky abstractions (exposing layer internals)                            â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Circular dependencies between layers                                     â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Business logic in presentation layer                                     â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Database concerns leaking into business layer                            â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚

â”‚   1. DECLARATIVE (Annotations/Attributes)                       â”‚
â”‚      â€¢ @Transactional on service method                         â”‚
â”‚      â€¢ Framework handles begin/commit/rollback                  â”‚
â”‚      â€¢ Simple and common approach                               â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   2. PROGRAMMATIC (Manual control)                              â”‚
â”‚      â€¢ Explicit begin/commit/rollback calls                     â”‚
â”‚      â€¢ More control, more code                                  â”‚
â”‚      â€¢ Use when declarative isn't flexible enough               â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   3. UNIT OF WORK PATTERN                                       â”‚
â”‚      â€¢ Track all changes in memory                              â”‚
â”‚      â€¢ Commit all changes at once                               â”‚
â”‚      â€¢ Common with ORMs                                         â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TRANSACTION BEST PRACTICES:                                   â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                   â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âœ“ Keep transactions short                                     â”‚
â”‚   âœ“ One transaction per use case (usually)                      â”‚
â”‚   âœ“ Don't span transactions across service calls                â”‚
â”‚   âœ“ Handle failures gracefully                                  â”‚
â”‚   âœ“ Be careful with async operations in transactions            â”‚
â”‚   âœ“ Avoid transactions for read-only operations                 â”‚

â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                     â”‚

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚              APPLICATION LAYER OPTIMIZATION TIPS                 â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 1: ONE USE CASE = ONE CLASS                               â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                               â”‚
â”‚   Don't create "OrderService" with 50 methods                   â”‚
â”‚   Create PlaceOrderUseCase, CancelOrderUseCase, etc.            â”‚
â”‚   Single Responsibility at use case level                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   Benefits:                                                     â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Easier to understand                                        â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Easier to test                                              â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Clear dependencies per use case                             â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Can apply decorators per use case                           â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 2: USE COMMAND/QUERY OBJECTS                              â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                              â”‚
â”‚   Encapsulate use case input in dedicated objects               â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   PlaceOrderCommand {                                           â”‚
â”‚     customerId                                                  â”‚
â”‚     items[]                                                     â”‚
â”‚     shippingAddress                                             â”‚
â”‚   }                                                             â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   Benefits:                                                     â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Self-documenting                                            â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Can add validation                                          â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Easy to serialize/deserialize                               â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Works well with message queues                              â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 3: RETURN RESULT OBJECTS                                  â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                  â”‚
â”‚   Don't throw exceptions for business failures                  â”‚
â”‚   Return Result<Success, Failure> objects                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   Result<OrderPlaced, OrderError>                               â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Success: contains order ID, confirmation                    â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Failure: contains error code, message                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   Benefits:                                                     â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Explicit error handling                                     â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ No hidden control flow                                      â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Better API documentation                                    â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 4: HANDLE EVENTS AFTER TRANSACTION                        â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                        â”‚
â”‚   Collect domain events during use case                         â”‚
â”‚   Publish after transaction commits                             â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚

â”‚   Application layer = orchestration only                        â”‚
â”‚   If logic is complex, it probably belongs in domain            â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   Typical use case steps:                                       â”‚
â”‚   1. Validate authorization                                     â”‚
â”‚   2. Load domain objects                                        â”‚
â”‚   3. Call domain method(s)                                      â”‚

â”‚   5. Publish events                                             â”‚
â”‚   6. Return result                                              â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 6: USE INTERFACES FOR DEPENDENCIES                        â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                        â”‚
â”‚   Application layer depends on interfaces                       â”‚
â”‚   Infrastructure implements interfaces                          â”‚
â”‚   Enables testing with mocks                                    â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 7: CONSIDER CQRS SEPARATION                               â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                               â”‚
â”‚   Separate command handlers from query handlers                 â”‚
â”‚   Queries can bypass domain layer for performance               â”‚
â”‚   Commands always go through domain                             â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”

â”‚   1. Always immutable                                           â”‚

â”‚   DEFINITION:                                                   â”‚
â”‚   A cluster of domain objects (entities and value objects)      â”‚
â”‚   that can be treated as a single unit. Has a root entity       â”‚
â”‚   (Aggregate Root) that controls access to the cluster.         â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   PURPOSE:                                                      â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Define consistency boundaries                               â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Simplify complex object graphs                              â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Control access and enforce invariants                       â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Define transaction boundaries                               â”‚

â”‚   RULE 1: Reference aggregate roots only                        â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                        â”‚

â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   RULE 2: Modify through root only                              â”‚

â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âŒ Wrong: orderItem.setQuantity(5)                            â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Right: order.updateItemQuantity(itemId, 5)                 â”‚

â”‚   Each transaction modifies only one aggregate                  â”‚
â”‚   Use domain events for cross-aggregate updates                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   RULE 4: Reference other aggregates by ID                      â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                      â”‚

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚              DOMAIN LAYER OPTIMIZATION TIPS                      â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤

â”‚   TIP 1: RICH DOMAIN MODEL (Avoid Anemic)                       â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âŒ ANEMIC DOMAIN MODEL (Anti-pattern):                        â”‚
â”‚   Entity has only getters/setters                               â”‚
â”‚   All logic in services                                         â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   class Order {                                                 â”‚
â”‚     getId(), setId()                                            â”‚
â”‚     getStatus(), setStatus()  // Anyone can set anything!       â”‚
â”‚     getItems(), setItems()                                      â”‚
â”‚   }                                                             â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   class OrderService {                                          â”‚
â”‚     cancelOrder(order) {                                        â”‚
â”‚       if (order.getStatus() == SHIPPED) throw...                â”‚
â”‚       order.setStatus(CANCELLED)  // Logic outside entity       â”‚
â”‚     }                                                           â”‚
â”‚   }                                                             â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âœ… RICH DOMAIN MODEL:                                         â”‚
â”‚   Entity encapsulates behavior                                  â”‚
â”‚   Business rules inside entity                                  â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   class Order {                                                 â”‚
â”‚     // No public setters!                                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚     cancel(reason: CancelReason): void {                        â”‚
â”‚       if (this.status == SHIPPED) {                             â”‚
â”‚         throw new CannotCancelShippedOrder()                    â”‚
â”‚       }                                                         â”‚
â”‚       this.status = CANCELLED                                   â”‚
â”‚       this.cancelReason = reason                                â”‚
â”‚       this.addEvent(new OrderCancelled(...))                    â”‚
â”‚     }                                                           â”‚
â”‚   }                                                             â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 2: MAKE INVALID STATES UNREPRESENTABLE                    â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                    â”‚

â”‚   TIP 3: USE UBIQUITOUS LANGUAGE                                â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                â”‚

â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 4: ENCAPSULATE COLLECTIONS                                â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                â”‚
â”‚   Don't expose internal collections                             â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âŒ Exposed collection:                                        â”‚
â”‚   order.getItems().add(newItem)  // Bypasses validation!        â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Encapsulated:                                              â”‚
â”‚   order.addItem(product, quantity)  // Validates, raises event  â”‚
â”‚   order.getItems()  // Returns immutable copy                   â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 5: FAIL FAST WITH DOMAIN EXCEPTIONS                       â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                       â”‚

â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   Better than generic exceptions:                               â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Self-documenting                                            â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Can be handled specifically                                 â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Carry domain-relevant information                           â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TIP 6: TEST DOMAIN IN ISOLATION                               â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                               â”‚
â”‚   Domain has no dependencies                                    â”‚
â”‚   Tests are pure unit tests                                     â”‚
â”‚   No mocks needed (usually)                                     â”‚
â”‚   Fast, reliable, easy to write                                 â”‚

4.5 Data Access Layer (Deep Dive)

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”

â”‚   PRACTICE 1: MAKE IT WORK FIRST                                â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                â”‚
â”‚   Don't evolve architecture during initial development          â”‚
â”‚   Get the system working, then optimize                         â”‚
â”‚   "Make it work, make it right, make it fast"                   â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   PRACTICE 2: EVOLVE INCREMENTALLY                              â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                              â”‚
â”‚   Small steps, not big bang                                     â”‚
â”‚   Each step should be deployable and rollback-able              â”‚
â”‚   Celebrate small wins                                          â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   PRACTICE 3: INVEST IN AUTOMATED TESTING                       â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                       â”‚
â”‚   Tests give confidence to refactor                             â”‚
â”‚   Without tests, refactoring is risky                           â”‚
â”‚   Build test suite before major changes                         â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   PRACTICE 4: MONITOR EVERYTHING                                â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                â”‚
â”‚   Know your current performance baseline                        â”‚
â”‚   Compare before and after each change                          â”‚
â”‚   Detect problems early                                         â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   PRACTICE 5: HAVE A ROLLBACK PLAN                              â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                              â”‚
â”‚   Every change should be reversible                             â”‚
â”‚   Feature flags for gradual rollout                             â”‚
â”‚   Blue-green or canary deployments                              â”‚

4.11 Section Summary and Key Takeaways

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚               KEY TAKEAWAYS - SECTION 4                          â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   LAYERED ARCHITECTURE FUNDAMENTALS:                            â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Layers separate concerns horizontally                      â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Dependencies flow downward only                            â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Each layer has specific responsibilities                   â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Layers communicate through defined interfaces              â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   PRESENTATION LAYER:                                           â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Handles HTTP/UI concerns only                              â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Keep controllers thin                                      â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Use DTOs to decouple from domain                           â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Apply cross-cutting via middleware                         â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   APPLICATION LAYER:                                            â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Orchestrates use cases                                     â”‚
â”‚   âœ… One use case = one class                                   â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Manages transactions                                       â”‚
â”‚   âœ… No business logic (delegate to domain)                     â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   DOMAIN LAYER:                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Contains all business logic                                â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Rich domain model (not anemic)                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Entities, Value Objects, Aggregates                        â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Zero external dependencies                                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   DATA ACCESS LAYER:                                            â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Abstracts persistence                                      â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Repository pattern for aggregates                          â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Handle mapping between domain and DB                       â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Optimize queries (avoid N+1)                               â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   INFRASTRUCTURE LAYER:                                         â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Implements domain interfaces                               â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Wrap external services                                     â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Apply resilience patterns                                  â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Use Anti-Corruption Layer                                  â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   CRITICAL ANTI-PATTERNS TO AVOID:                              â”‚
â”‚   âš ï¸ Business logic in presentation                             â”‚
â”‚   âš ï¸ Anemic domain model                                        â”‚
â”‚   âš ï¸ Skipping layers                                            â”‚
â”‚   âš ï¸ Circular dependencies                                      â”‚
â”‚   âš ï¸ N+1 queries                                                â”‚
â”‚   âš ï¸ God services/classes                                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   TESTING STRATEGY:                                             â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Domain: Pure unit tests                                    â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Application: Unit tests with mocks                         â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Infrastructure: Integration tests                          â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Presentation: HTTP integration tests                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   EVOLUTION PRINCIPLES:                                         â”‚
â”‚   âœ… Evolve when you feel real pain                             â”‚

Ready for Section 5?

Section 5: Microservices Architecture (Deep Dive) will cover:

  • Common Pitfalls and How to Avoid Them
